***pearly.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:pearly.html>pearly</a> (59660)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">pearl</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">-y</i>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:pearly.html>pearly</a></strong> (<i>countable and uncountable</i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">pearlies</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">uncountable<span class="ib-comma">,</span> uncommon<span class="ib-comma">,</span> dated</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A pale greyish white colour, tinted with blue.
<dl><dd><div class="color-panel"><a href = vnd.unilang:pearly.html>pearly</a> colour: <span style="background-color:E5E1D4; display:inline-block; width:80px;"> </span></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1830</b>,  John Burnet,  <cite>A practical treatise on painting</cite>, page 3:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">In nature <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> as often find the light <a href = vnd.unilang:cool.html>cool</a> as <a href = vnd.unilang:warm.html>warm</a>; also in the pictures of many of the Flemish and Dutch schools, where, as <a href = vnd.unilang:sir.html>Sir</a> Joshua himself mentions, " the silver gray or <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pearly.html>pearly</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> predominant, and are valued by the connoisseurs in proportion as they possess this excellence of a silver tint."</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1884</b>,  <cite>The popular educator‎</cite>, page 49:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:pearly.html>Pearly</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> that <a href = vnd.unilang:silky.html>silky</a> and often coloured lustre which renders of such value</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1899</b>,  <cite>St. <a href = vnd.unilang:louis.html>Louis</a> medical and surgical journal‎</cite>, page 126:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">When (the scales are) more developed and thickened, the color (<b><a href = vnd.unilang:pearly.html>pearly</a></b>) <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> deepened, shading</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">countable<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> especially in plural</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A tooth.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjective">Adjective</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:pearly.html>pearly</a></strong> (<i>comparative</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en comparative-form-of" lang="en">pearlier</b>, <i>superlative</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en superlative-form-of" lang="en">pearliest</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Of a pale greyish white colour, tinted with blue.</li>
<li>Resembling or characteristic of a pearl; nacreous.
<dl><dd><i>a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pearly.html>pearly</a></b> lustre</i></dd></dl></li>
<li>Containing or yielding pearls.</li>
<li>Having a pure sweet tone.</li></ol>
</body>

***pech.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:pech.html>pech</a> (2778)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:pech.html>Pech</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">bad luck; pitch, tar</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">peh</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">pīx</i>. Doublet of inherited <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:pek.html>pek</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">pitch</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Also cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">pitch</i>.
</p><p>The sense “breakdown” <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a Dutch innovation. It <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> probably modelled on the word <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ongeluk.html>ongeluk</a></i>, which means both “bad look, misfortune” and “accident”. Since <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:pech.html>pech</a></i> typically denotes a lesser <a href = vnd.unilang:kind.html>kind</a> of bad luck, it <a href = vnd.unilang:came.html>came</a> to be used for a lesser <a href = vnd.unilang:kind.html>kind</a> of traffic accident too. German uses <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:panne.html>Panne</a></i> instead; compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:panne.html>panne</a></i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:pech.html>pech</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>uncountable</i>)
</p>
<ol><li>bad luck; bad <a href = vnd.unilang:karma.html>karma</a></li>
<li>breakdown, e.g. of a car</li></ol>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zelfstandig_naamwoord"><i><a href = vnd.unilang:zelfstandig.html>Zelfstandig</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:naamwoord.html>naamwoord</a></i></span></h4>
<p><b><a href = vnd.unilang:pech.html>pech</a></b> <span style="background-color: f8f9fa;border-radius: 2px;border: 1px solid c8ccd1;padding: 0 0.2em 0 0.1em;font-style: italic">m</span>
</p>
<ol><li><a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:conditie.html>conditie</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:waarin.html>waarin</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:er.html>er</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:tegenslag.html>tegenslag</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:te.html>te</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:verwerken.html>verwerken</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:die.html>die</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:door.html>door</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:eigen.html>eigen</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:schuld.html>schuld</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:veroorzaakt.html>veroorzaakt</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a>
<dl><dd><ul><li><i><a href = vnd.unilang:vorig.html>Vorig</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:jaar.html>jaar</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:wilde.html>wilde</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>hij</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:medicijnen.html>medicijnen</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:gaan.html>gaan</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:studeren.html>studeren</a>, <a href = vnd.unilang:maar.html>maar</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>hij</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:enorme.html>enorme</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pech.html>pech</a></b> want <a href = vnd.unilang:ondanks.html>ondanks</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:acht.html>acht</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:gemiddeld.html>gemiddeld</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:kwam.html>kwam</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>hij</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:door.html>door</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:loting.html>loting</a>.</i> </li></ul></dd></dl></li></ol>

***peck.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> peck (10923)</h1><br></body> 
***pecker.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a> (68108)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">pekker</i>, equivalent to <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">peck</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to pick at something in the manner of a bird</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:dictatoriaal.html>-er</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">forming <a href = vnd.unilang:agent.html>agent</a> nouns</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">peckers</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Someone who or something that pecks, striking or piercing in the manner of a bird's beak or bill, particularly:
<ul><li><b>2003 October 18</b>, <i>The Economist</i>, "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.economist.com/node/2138027">Stress Test</a>"
<dl><dd>Two studies of British civil servants, for example, suggest that those at the top of the heap are less stressed than those near the bottom. Work on other species, too, indicates that when it <a href = vnd.unilang:comes.html>comes</a> to pecking <a href = vnd.unilang:orders.html>orders</a>, the peckees are more stressed than the <b>peckers</b>.</dd></dl></li></ul>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">uncommon  or  regional</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Any tool used in a pecking fashion, particularly <a href = vnd.unilang:kinds.html>kinds</a> of <a href = vnd.unilang:hoes.html>hoes</a> or pickaxes.
<ul><li><b>1588</b>, Thomas Hariot, <i>A Briefe and True Report of the New Found <a href = vnd.unilang:land.html>Land</a> of Virginia</i>, sig. C2:
<dl><dd>The women with short <b>peckers</b> or parers,... of a <a href = vnd.unilang:foote.html>foote</a> long and about fiue <a href = vnd.unilang:inches.html>inches</a> in breadth: <a href = vnd.unilang:doe.html>doe</a> onely breake the vpper part of the ground to rayse vp the weedes, <a href = vnd.unilang:grasse.html>grasse</a>, amp; old stubbes of corne stalkes with their rootes... For their corne,... with a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b> they make a hole, wherein they put foure graines.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1782</b>, J. Scott, <i>Poetical Works</i>, page 119:
<dl><dd>Let sturdy youths their pointed <b>peckers</b> ply,</dd>
<dd>Till the <a href = vnd.unilang:rais.html>rais</a>'d roots loose on the surface lie.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1848</b>, <i>Journal of the Royal Agricultural Society</i>, 9 ii. 551:
<dl><dd>A small narrow <a href = vnd.unilang:hoe.html>hoe</a> or <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>... A small <b>hand-pecker</b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1948</b>, M. Carbery amp; E. Grey, <i>Hertfordshire Heritage</i>, page 120:
<dl><dd><i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>Pecker</a></b></i>, small pickaxe for cutting furze.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">uncommon</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Any machine or machine part moving in a pecking fashion, particularly:
<ul><li><b>1922</b>, <i>Whittaker's Mechanical Engineer's Pocket Book</i>, page 368:
<dl><dd>The upper end of the finger <i><a href = vnd.unilang:o.html>o</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:carries.html>carries</a> a "<b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>" <i>p</i>, which consists of a hardened steel piece with a V edge. This <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> engaged by any one of several <a href = vnd.unilang:steps.html>steps</a> or notches in a stepped block <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> carried by the <a href = vnd.unilang:rocking.html>rocking</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:lever.html>lever</a> <i>l</i>.</dd></dl></li></ul>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">weaving<span class="ib-comma">,</span> obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <a href = vnd.unilang:picker.html>picker</a>, a shuttle-driver: the device which <a href = vnd.unilang:moves.html>moves</a> backwards and <a href = vnd.unilang:forwards.html>forwards</a> in the shuttle-box to drive the shuttle through the warp.
<ul><li><b>1807</b>, Thomas Johnson, British Patent № 3023 (1856), 5:
<dl><dd>The shuttle... receives its motion from the <b>peckers</b> connected with cords pulled by the <b>pecking</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:lever.html>lever</a>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1878</b>, Alfred Barlow, <i>The History and Principles of Weaving by Hand and by Power</i>, x. 136:
<dl><dd>When the shaft [of the draw-boy] rocks from side to side of the machine, it will carry the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>... with it.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">telegraphy<span class="ib-comma">,</span> historical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <a href = vnd.unilang:kind.html>kind</a> of V-shaped telegraphic relay.
<ul><li><b>1858 June 13</b>, H.C.F. Jenkin, letter in <i>Papers</i> (1887), volume I, page lxxxvi:
<dl><dd>Click, click, click, the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> at work.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1940</b>, <i>Chambers's Technical Dictionary</i>, 621/1:
<dl><dd><i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>Pecker</a></b></i>, the small cylindrical pin which rises and falls in <a href = vnd.unilang:scanning.html>scanning</a> the <a href = vnd.unilang:holes.html>holes</a> punched in a slip corresponding to the coding of the message.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a>  regional<span class="ib-comma">,</span> historical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Clipping of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a> mill</i></span></span>, a rice mill.
<ul><li><b>1802</b>, J. Drayton, <i>A view of South Carolina, as respects her natural and civil <a href = vnd.unilang:concerns.html>concerns</a></i>, page 121:
<dl><dd>Rice mills, called <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>, cog, and water <b>mills</b>... The first... so called, from the pestle's striking... in the manner of a wood <a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1949</b>, S. C. Murray, <i>This Our <a href = vnd.unilang:land.html>Land</a>: the Story of the Agricultural Society of South Carolina</i>, page 41:
<dl><dd>After being thrashed by flail or whipped off, the rice <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> milled and dressed wholly by hand or by a crude machine called a ‘<b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>’.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">zoology</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A bird, particularly a member of the group of <a href = vnd.unilang:birds.html>birds</a> including the berrypeckers, flowerpeckers, and woodpeckers.
<ul><li><b>1697</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Dryden" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:John Dryden">John Dryden</a> translating <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Publius_Virgilius_Maro" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Publius Virgilius Maro">Publius Virgilius Maro</a> as <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgics" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Georgics">Georgics</a></i>, iv:
<dl><dd>The Titmouse, and the <b>Peckers</b> hungry <a href = vnd.unilang:brood.html>Brood</a>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1884 January</b>, George <a href = vnd.unilang:allen.html>Allen</a> in <i>Longman's Magazine</i>, page 294:
<dl><dd>By far the greater number of modern <a href = vnd.unilang:birds.html>birds</a> belong to the... <a href = vnd.unilang:orders.html>orders</a> of the perchers, the <b>peckers</b>, and the <a href = vnd.unilang:birds.html>birds</a> of prey.</dd></dl></li></ul>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">zoology<span class="ib-comma">,</span> usually  colloquial  or  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a>  regional</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Clipping of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">woodpecker</i></span></span> (Picidae).
<ul><li><b>1883</b>, J.S. Stallybrass translating <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_Grimm" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Jacob Grimm"><a href = vnd.unilang:jacob.html>Jacob</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:grimm.html>Grimm</a></a> as <i>Teutonic Mythology</i>, volume III, page 973:
<dl><dd>The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> esteemed a sacred and divine bird.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1980</b> January 20, <i>Washington Post</i>, m1:
<dl><dd>I've <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> feeding several downy <b>’peckers</b> from my short-perched <a href = vnd.unilang:tubes.html>tubes</a> for years.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  regional<span class="ib-comma">,</span> obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> An eater, a <a href = vnd.unilang:diner.html>diner</a>.
<ul><li><b>1862</b>, C.C. Robinson, <i>The Dialect of Leeds amp; Its Neighbourhood</i>, page 383:
<dl><dd>He's a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:rare.html>rare</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1873</b>, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>Slang</a> Dictionary</i>:
<dl><dd><i>Peck</i>... A hearty eater <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> generally called ‘a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:rare.html>rare</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>’.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1894</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:mrs.html>Mrs</a>. H. Ward, <i>Marcella</i>, II. iv. v. 476:
<dl><dd>But I've <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> better iver since, an' beginnin' to eat my vittles, too, though I'm never no great <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  regional</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A bird's beak or bill.
<ul><li><b>1891</b>, G. Sweetman, <i>A Glossary of <a href = vnd.unilang:words.html>Words</a> used by the rural population in the parish and neighbourhood of Wincanton, Somerset</i>:
<dl><dd><i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>Pecker</a></b></i>, a bird's bill</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1967</b>, H. Orton amp; M. F. Wakelin, <i>A Survey of English dialects</i> B, volume 4:
<dl><dd>Q. What does a bird peck its food up with?... [Wiltshire] Beak, <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">chiefly <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> regional<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <a href = vnd.unilang:penis.html>penis</a>; cock, <a href = vnd.unilang:dick.html>dick</a>.
<ul><li><b>1902</b>, J. S. Farmer amp; W. E. Henley, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>Slang</a> and Its Analogues</i> (London), V. 289/2:
<dl><dd>The <a href = vnd.unilang:penis.html>penis</a>... <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1936</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Miller" class="extiw" title="w:Henry Miller"><a href = vnd.unilang:henry.html>Henry</a> Miller</a>,  “The Tailor Shop”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Spring_(novel)" class="extiw" title="w:Black Spring (novel)">Black Spring</a></cite>, Paris |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obelisk_Press" class="extiw" title="w:Obelisk Press">The <a href = vnd.unilang:obelisk.html>Obelisk</a> Press</a><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="338, rue Saint-Honoré">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/459562537">459562537</a></small> |  republished New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grove_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Grove Press">Grove Press</a>, 1963, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/blackspring00millpage/126/mode/1up">pages 125–126</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Ought to stand on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Square" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Times Square">Times Square</a> with my <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b> in my hand and piss in the gutter.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1964</b>, <i>American Folk Music Occasional</i>, i. 12:
<dl><dd>There <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a house down in New Orleans,</dd>
<dd>They call it <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_the_Rising_Sun" class="extiw" title="w:House of the Rising Sun">The <a href = vnd.unilang:rising.html>Rising</a> Sun</a>,</dd>
<dd>When you want to get your <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b> spoilt,</dd>
<dd>That's where you get it done.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1990 Fall</b>, <i>Paris Review</i>, volume 32, number 116, page 171:
<dl><dd>He <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> the <b>biggest <a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a> in the pool</b>, politically speaking.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  colloquial<span class="ib-comma">,</span> by extension  of  the sense   | beak | </span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A nose.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a>  colloquial<span class="ib-comma">,</span> by extension<span class="ib-comma">,</span> from the expression  | keep one's <a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a> up | </span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:spirits.html>Spirits</a>, nerve, courage.
<ul><li><b>1845 September 15</b>, <i>Times</i> (London), 8/3:
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:mr.html>Mr</a>. King... misstated the fact in saying that he <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> put a piece of lighted paper to the master's nose while asleep in that house; it <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> his hot pipe that he applied to the sleeper's nostrils, at the same time <a href = vnd.unilang:crying.html>crying</a>: Come, old chap, <b>keep your <a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a> up</b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1873</b>, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>Slang</a> Dictionary</i>:
<dl><dd><i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>Pecker</a></b></i>, ‘<b>keep your <a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>Pecker</a> up</b>’,... literally, keep your beak and head well up, ‘never say <a href = vnd.unilang:die.html>die</a>’.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1875</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W.S._Gilbert" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:W.S. Gilbert">W.S. <a href = vnd.unilang:gilbert.html>Gilbert</a></a>, <i>Trial by <a href = vnd.unilang:jury.html>Jury</a></i>, 4:
<dl><dd>Be firm, my moral <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1900</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Conrad" class="extiw" title="w:Joseph Conrad">Joseph Conrad</a>, <i>Lord <a href = vnd.unilang:jim.html>Jim</a></i>, ch 5:
<dl><dd>... he <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> every facility given him to remain under lock and key, with a chair, a table, a mattress in a corner, and a litter of fallen plaster on the floor, in an irrational state of funk, and <a href = vnd.unilang:keeping.html>keeping</a> up his <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a></b> with such <a href = vnd.unilang:tonics.html>tonics</a> as Mariani dispensed.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2003</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J.K._Rowling" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:J.K. Rowling">J.K. Rowling</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix"><a href = vnd.unilang:harry.html>Harry</a> Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i>, page xii:
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:fred.html>Fred</a> and I managed to <b>keep our peckers up</b> somehow.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">chiefly  in the plural<span class="ib-comma">,</span> derogatory  <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <i>Short for</i> <b>peckerwood</b> ("<a href = vnd.unilang:whitey.html>whitey</a>; white trash")
<ul><li><b>1966</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:r.html>R</a>.G. Toepfer, <i>Witness</i>, xvi. 127:
<dl><dd>These <b>peckers</b> know that as well as <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1971</b>, D. Wells amp; S. Dance, <i>Night People</i>, i. 7:
<dl><dd>Those <a href = vnd.unilang:cats.html>cats</a> wouldn'<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> let us get five <a href = vnd.unilang:feet.html>feet</a> from the Y.M.C.A. Like real <b>peckers</b>, they'd say, ‘If I <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> you <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_South" class="extiw" title="w:American South">down South</a>.’</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">chiefly  in the plural<span class="ib-comma">,</span> derogatory  <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <i>Short for</i> <b>peckerhead</b> ("dickhead; an aggressive or objectionable idiot").
<ul><li><b>2013</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:sean.html>Sean</a> Moore, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.co.uk/books?id=FJEg5NI4vdQCamp;pg=PT41">"<a href = vnd.unilang:sat.html>Sat</a> Phone Black <a href = vnd.unilang:op.html>Op</a>" in <i>Outside the Wire</i>, 41</a>:
<dl><dd>Goddammit! I give you <b>peckers</b> an inch and you automatically take a mile <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Clipping of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:pecker.html>pecker</a> head</i></span></span> ("an electric <a href = vnd.unilang:motor.html>motor</a>'s junction or terminal connection box, where power cords are connected to the <a href = vnd.unilang:winding.html>winding</a> leads").</li></ol>

***pedagogiek.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:pedagogiek.html>pedagogiek</a> (89456)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:pedagogiek.html>pedagogiek</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>uncountable</i>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">pedagogy</span></li></ol>

***peddel.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:peddel.html>peddel</a> (23379)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">paddle</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:peddel.html>peddel</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:peddels.html>peddels</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:peddel.html>peddeltje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>A paddle, two-handed, single-bladed oar which isn'<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> fixed to the boat but hand-held</li>
<li>A spanking paddle</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li>(oar) <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:paddel.html>paddel</a></span> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:riem.html>riem</a></span> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:roeiriem.html>roeiriem</a></span> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:roeispaan.html>roeispaan</a></span> (less specific)</li>
<li>(spanking implement) <span class="Latn" lang="nl">paddle</span> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span></li></ul>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:peeling.html>peeling</a> (80476)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:peeling.html>peeling</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">peelings</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>The act of removing the outer surface in <a href = vnd.unilang:strips.html>strips</a>.
<ul><li><b>1847</b>, <i>Food for the Million. Maize against potato</i>
<dl><dd>In the culinary process, there are none of those <b>peelings</b> and washings as in the case of potatoes and turnips, <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> none of those squeezings and mashings and choppings, before the worthless mess can be got upon the table.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><a href = vnd.unilang:strips.html>Strips</a> of an outer rind or surface that <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> removed.
<dl><dd><i>She flavored the broth with vegetable <b>peelings</b>.</i></dd></dl></li></ol>

***peen.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:peen.html>peen</a> (89453)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Originally the plural of <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">pee</i>, perhaps from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">*pede</i>, with plural <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">peden</i> (with a single attestation), of uncertain origin. Compare <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:schoen.html>schoen</a></i> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">teen</i>, also originally plurals but <a href = vnd.unilang:later.html>later</a> singulars. Proposed cognates include <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">pith</i> and <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr"><a href = vnd.unilang:pied.html>pied</a></i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_4">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:peen.html>peen</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:peen.html>penen</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:peentje.html>peentje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)

***pees.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:pees.html>pees</a> (31008)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1_2">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">pese</i>.  See <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:vezel.html>vezel</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">fiber, sinew</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_4">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:pees.html>pees</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:pezen.html>pezen</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:pees.html>peesje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>A sinew.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>See the etymology of the main entry.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb_2">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

***pekel.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:pekel.html>pekel</a> (63469)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">peeckel</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:pekelen.html>pekele</a></i>. The word <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> originally restricted to Dutch and Low German; compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Low_German" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Low German">Middle Low German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gml">pēkel</i>. From these two languages are borrowed <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">pickle</i> and <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Pökel</i>. Further origin uncertain. A relation with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">piquer</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">piquant</i> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> sometimes supposed.
</p>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">pēnis</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">tail, <a href = vnd.unilang:penis.html>penis</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*pes-</i>.

***penn.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> penn (6729)</h1><br></body> 
***pennant.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:pennant.html>pennant</a> (73605)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">penon</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">penoun</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">pynoun</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">penon</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">pennon</i>, from <span id="attentionseekingla" class="attentionseeking" lang="la"></span> <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">penna</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">feather</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. See <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:pen.html>pen</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">a feather</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, and compare <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">pennon</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">pinion</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:pennant.html>pennant</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">pennants</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A flag normally used by naval vessels to represent a special condition.
<ol><li>The broad <a href = vnd.unilang:pennant.html>pennant</a> flown by <a href = vnd.unilang:commodores.html>commodores</a>.</li>
<li>The church <a href = vnd.unilang:pennant.html>pennant</a> indicating religious services are taking place aboard ship.</li>
<li>The commissioning <a href = vnd.unilang:pennant.html>pennant</a> flown on ceremonial <a href = vnd.unilang:occasions.html>occasions</a>.</li></ol></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">sports</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The winning of a competition, represented by a flag.
<dl><dd><i>The New York <a href = vnd.unilang:yankees.html>Yankees</a> have <a href = vnd.unilang:won.html>won</a> the American League <b><a href = vnd.unilang:pennant.html>pennant</a></b> far more often than any other team.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li>A rope or strap to which a purchase <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> hooked.</li>
<li>A sandstone between coal measures in parts of South Wales</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p>Not to be confused with <a href = vnd.unilang:pedant.html>pedant</a> (one overly concerned with correctness), nor with pendant (a piece of jewellery).
</p>

<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">pennon</span></li></ul>
</body>

***penning.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:penning.html>penning</a> (5550)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">penninc</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">pennink</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*panningaz</i>. <span class="maintenance-line"><i>This etymology <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> incomplete. You can help Wiktionary by elaborating on the origins of this term.</i></span>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_4">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:penning.html>penning</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:penningen.html>penningen</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:penning.html>penninkje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">historical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A small coin, usually made of silver but <a href = vnd.unilang:later.html>later</a> also of gold; <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:penny.html>penny</a></span>.</li>
<li>A medal or commemoration coin.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">figuratively</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">money</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">cash</span>.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">coin</span>.</li></ol>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:pens.html>pens</a> (23378)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:pense.html>pense</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">panse</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">belly; tripe</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">pantex</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">belly; <a href = vnd.unilang:guts.html>guts</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">paunch</i>.
</p>
